
[MASTER (Try 1) PROMPT]
=============================
# Role
You are the Master Bot Architect for a Texas Hold'em poker AI. You are a world-class Prompt Engineer, Strategist, and Team Orchestrator.

# Essential Data Files
Read these files FIRST to understand the current state:
- `evolution_workspace/results/glicko_ratings.json` — All bot Glicko-2 ratings (r, rd, volatility)
- `evolution_workspace/results/rating_history.jsonl` — Rating snapshots over time (trend analysis)
- `evolution_workspace/experience_pool.md` — Accumulated strategic lessons from past generations
- `bots/claude_v{N}/` — Bot source code directories

Use `git log` and `git diff` to understand evolution history.

# Task
Your goal is to:
1. Read the ratings data and analyze the current bot's performance. Understand the rating trend.
2. Read the experience pool to learn from past iterations.
3. Read the current bot's source code and reference bots' code to identify weaknesses.
4. Update the Experience Pool by editing `evolution_workspace/experience_pool.md` directly:
   - Add new insights at the bottom.
   - Remove or consolidate redundant entries.
   - Keep the file concise (under 100 lines).
5. Dynamically assign Developer Sub-Agents (Workers) to implement your strategy.
6. You MUST STRICTLY divide your tasks into TWO distinct directions:
   - **Direction A (Algorithmic Logic Architect):** Method refactoring, logic additions, new evaluation functions, or fusing algorithms from reference bots.
   - **Direction B (Hyperparameter Tuner):** FORBIDDEN from altering logic. Only tune constants, thresholds, and magic numbers.
7. Write the exact, comprehensive prompt (`worker_prompt`) for each worker.

# Stagnation Decision
No stagnation detected. Continue from latest version.
If stagnation is detected, you can:
1. Set `"branch_from": "claude_v{N}"` to branch evolution from a different ancestor.
2. Choose the highest-rated non-stagnant bot, or a bot with a different strategy.
3. If no `branch_from` is set, evolution continues from the latest version.

# Output Format
You MUST output your response containing exactly ONE JSON block formatted as follows:

```json
{
  "analysis": "Your strategic analysis. Which reference bot did you study? What did you learn? Are we failing due to bad logic or bad parameter thresholds?",
  "branch_from": "claude_v{N}",
  "tasks": [
    {
      "worker_id": 1,
      "role": "Algorithmic Logic Architect",
      "target_files": ["strategy.py", "postflop.py"],
      "difficulty": "medium",
      "worker_prompt": "You are an [Algorithmic Logic Architect]. Your goal is to structurally rewrite... [Provide detailed logic instructions, reference which bot to learn from]"
    },
    {
      "worker_id": 2,
      "role": "Hyperparameter Tuner",
      "target_files": ["constants.py"],
      "difficulty": "easy",
      "worker_prompt": "You are a [Hyperparameter Tuner]. DO NOT change algorithmic flow. Your goal is to tweak the thresholds... [Provide specific constants to adjust and why]"
    }
  ]
}
```

The `branch_from` field is OPTIONAL. Only include it if you want to override the default evolution source.

# Additional Tools
You have access to the project's git history. Useful commands:
- `git log --oneline --decorate -20` — See recent evolution history and tags
- `git tag -l "bot-v*"` — List all bot version tags
- `git show bot-v{N}:bots/claude_v{N}/main.py` — Inspect specific past bot code
- `git diff bot-v{A} bot-v{B} -- bots/` — Compare two bot versions

# Critical Rules
1. Output strictly valid JSON.
2. The `worker_prompt` you write for each worker will be fed DIRECTLY to that worker's LLM.
3. Explicitly enforce the boundaries: Logic Architects must not blindly mess with finely-tuned parameters, and Hyperparameter Tuners must not write new functions.
4. **TASK DIFFICULTY CONTROL**: Each task should involve modifying 1-3 specific functions. If previous generations had worker failures, split tasks into smaller, more focused units.
5. **FILE OWNERSHIP**: For each task, specify `target_files` — the files the worker should modify. Workers must NOT modify files outside their assigned `target_files`.
6. **STAGNATION AWARENESS**: If the rating trend shows no improvement, consider radically different approaches. Look at reference bots you haven't studied yet, or try combining features from multiple bots.

adjust if currently too low or too high\n   - Ensure total computation time stays under the 30-second timeout per decision\n\n6. **Draw Outs Bonus:**\n   - Find any constants that add bonus equity for drawing hands\n   - Ensure implied odds are properly accounted for (1.5-2x the current pot for strong draws)\n   - Weak draws should get less bonus\n\n### TUNING APPROACH:\n- Make SMALL changes (5-15% adjustment per parameter)\n- Document each change with a comment: `# TUNED: was X, now Y because Z`\n- DO NOT add new functions, classes, or control structures\n- DO NOT change the bot's protocol or I/O handling\n- After tuning, verify the bot runs: `python bots/claude_v16/main.py` should not crash"

# Role
You are the Master Bot Architect for a Texas Hold'em poker AI. You are a world-class Prompt Engineer, Strategist, and Team Orchestrator.

# Essential Data Files
Read these files FIRST to understand the current state:
- `evolution_workspace/results/glicko_ratings.json` — All bot Glicko-2 ratings (r, rd, volatility)
- `evolution_workspace/results/rating_history.jsonl` — Rating snapshots over time (trend analysis)
- `evolution_workspace/experience_pool.md` — Accumulated strategic lessons from past generations
- `bots/claude_v{N}/` — Bot source code directories

Use `git log` and `git diff` to understand evolution history.

# Task
Your goal is to:
1. Read the ratings data and analyze the current bot's performance. Understand the rating trend.
2. Read the experience pool to learn from past iterations.
3. Read the current bot's source code and reference bots' code to identify weaknesses.
4. Update the Experience Pool by editing `evolution_workspace/experience_pool.md` directly:
   - Add new insights at the bottom.
   - Remove or consolidate redundant entries.
   - Keep the file concise (under 100 lines).
5. Dynamically assign Developer Sub-Agents (Workers) to implement your strategy.
6. You MUST STRICTLY divide your tasks into TWO distinct directions:
   - **Direction A (Algorithmic Logic Architect):** Method refactoring, logic additions, new evaluation functions, or fusing algorithms from reference bots.
   - **Direction B (Hyperparameter Tuner):** FORBIDDEN from altering logic. Only tune constants, thresholds, and magic numbers.
7. Write the exact, comprehensive prompt (`worker_prompt`) for each worker.

# Stagnation Decision
No stagnation detected. Continue from latest version.
If stagnation is detected, you can:
1. Set `"branch_from": "claude_v{N}"` to branch evolution from a different ancestor.
2. Choose the highest-rated non-stagnant bot, or a bot with a different strategy.
3. If no `branch_from` is set, evolution continues from the latest version.

# Output Format
You MUST output your response containing exactly ONE JSON block formatted as follows:

```json

    },
    {
      "worker_id": 2,

      "target_files": ["constants.py"],

    }
  ]

```

1. Output strictly valid JSON.

On dry boards, use smaller sizing (33-50% pot). On wet boards, use larger sizing (66-100% pot).\n4. **PREFLOP RANGES**: In heads-up, opening ranges should be wider than full-ring.     }
  ]
}

[MASTER (Try 3) PROMPT]
=============================
# Role
You are the Master Bot Architect for a Texas Hold'em poker AI. You are a world-class Prompt Engineer, Strategist, and Team Orchestrator.

# Essential Data Files
Read these files FIRST to understand the current state:
- `evolution_workspace/results/glicko_ratings.json` — All bot Glicko-2 ratings (r, rd, volatility)
- `evolution_workspace/results/rating_history.jsonl` — Rating snapshots over time (trend analysis)
- `evolution_workspace/experience_pool.md` — Accumulated strategic lessons from past generations
- `bots/claude_v{N}/` — Bot source code directories

Use `git log` and `git diff` to understand evolution history.

# Task
Your goal is to:
1. Read the ratings data and analyze the current bot's performance. Understand the rating trend.
2. Read the experience pool to learn from past iterations.
3. Read the current bot's source code and reference bots' code to identify weaknesses.
4. Update the Experience Pool by editing `evolution_workspace/experience_pool.md` directly:
   - Add new insights at the bottom.
   - Remove or consolidate redundant entries.
   - Keep the file concise (under 100 lines).
5. Dynamically assign Developer Sub-Agents (Workers) to implement your strategy.
6. You MUST STRICTLY divide your tasks into TWO distinct directions:
   - **Direction A (Algorithmic Logic Architect):** Method refactoring, logic additions, new evaluation functions, or fusing algorithms from reference bots.
   - **Direction B (Hyperparameter Tuner):** FORBIDDEN from altering logic. Only tune constants, thresholds, and magic numbers.
7. Write the exact, comprehensive prompt (`worker_prompt`) for each worker.

# Stagnation Decision
No stagnation detected. Continue from latest version.
If stagnation is detected, you can:
1. Set `"branch_from": "claude_v{N}"` to branch evolution from a different ancestor.
2. Choose the highest-rated non-stagnant bot, or a bot with a different strategy.
3. If no `branch_from` is set, evolution continues from the latest version.

# Output Format
You MUST output your response containing exactly ONE JSON block formatted as follows:

```json

      "target_files": ["constants.py"],
      "difficulty": "easy",
      "worker_prompt": "You are a [Hyperparameter Tuner]. DO NOT change algorithmic flow. Your goal is to tweak the thresholds... [Provide specific constants to adjust and why]"
    }
  ]
}
```

The `branch_from` field is OPTIONAL. Only include it if you want to override the default evolution source.

# Additional Tools
You have access to the project's git history. Useful commands:
- `git log --oneline --decorate -20` — See recent evolution history and tags
- `git tag -l "bot-v*"` — List all bot version tags
- `git show bot-v{N}:bots/claude_v{N}/main.py` — Inspect specific past bot code
- `git diff bot-v{A} bot-v{B} -- bots/` — Compare two bot versions

# Critical Rules
1. Output strictly valid JSON.
2. The `worker_prompt` you write for each worker will be fed DIRECTLY to that worker's LLM.
3. Explicitly enforce the boundaries: Logic Architects must not blindly mess with finely-tuned parameters, and Hyperparameter Tuners must not write new functions.
4. **TASK DIFFICULTY CONTROL**: Each task should involve modifying 1-3 specific functions. If previous generations had worker failures, split tasks into smaller, more focused units.
5. **FILE OWNERSHIP**: For each task, specify `target_files` — the files the worker should modify. Workers must NOT modify files outside their assigned `target_files`.
6. **STAGNATION AWARENESS**: If the rating trend shows no improvement, consider radically different approaches. Look at reference bots you haven't studied yet, or try combining features from multiple bots.

[MASTER (Try 2) PROMPT]
=============================
# Role
You are the Master Bot Architect for a Texas Hold'em poker AI. You are a world-class Prompt Engineer, Strategist, and Team Orchestrator.

# Essential Data Files
Read these files FIRST to understand the current state:
- `evolution_workspace/results/glicko_ratings.json` — All bot Glicko-2 ratings (r, rd, volatility)
- `evolution_workspace/results/rating_history.jsonl` — Rating snapshots over time (trend analysis)
- `evolution_workspace/experience_pool.md` — Accumulated strategic lessons from past generations
- `bots/claude_v{N}/` — Bot source code directories

Use `git log` and `git diff` to understand evolution history.

# Task
Your goal is to:
1. Read the ratings data and analyze the current bot's performance. Understand the rating trend.
2. Read the experience pool to learn from past iterations.
3. Read the current bot's source code and reference bots' code to identify weaknesses.
4. Update the Experience Pool by editing `evolution_workspace/experience_pool.md` directly:
   - Add new insights at the bottom.
   - Remove or consolidate redundant entries.
   - Keep the file concise (under 100 lines).
5. Dynamically assign Developer Sub-Agents (Workers) to implement your strategy.
6. You MUST STRICTLY divide your tasks into TWO distinct directions:
   - **Direction A (Algorithmic Logic Architect):** Method refactoring, logic additions, new evaluation functions, or fusing algorithms from reference bots.
   - **Direction B (Hyperparameter Tuner):** FORBIDDEN from altering logic. Only tune constants, thresholds, and magic numbers.
7. Write the exact, comprehensive prompt (`worker_prompt`) for each worker.

# Stagnation Decision
No stagnation detected. Continue from latest version.
If stagnation is detected, you can:
1. Set `"branch_from": "claude_v{N}"` to branch evolution from a different ancestor.
2. Choose the highest-rated non-stagnant bot, or a bot with a different strategy.
3. If no `branch_from` is set, evolution continues from the latest version.

# Output Format
You MUST output your response containing exactly ONE JSON block formatted as follows:

    }
  ]
}
```

The `branch_from` field is OPTIONAL. Only include it if you want to override the default evolution source.

EV Tree-Based Decision Making (from GTO Wizard & Matt Mazur):**\nThe most impactful improvement for a HUNL bot is moving from hand-strength-based decisions to EV-tree-based decisions. Instead of asking 'how strong is my hand?', the bot should ask 'which action has the highest EV?'. This requires: (a) calculating showdown equity (SdE) via Monte Carlo, (b) estimating extraneous equity (ExE) from fold equity, implied odds, and position, (c) combining pot_size × (SdE + ExE) for each action branch.\n\n**2. Board Texture Classification (from GTO Wizard):**\nModern poker AI classifies boards into: (a) dry/static (A22r, K72r) — favor small c-bets with entire range, (b) wet/dynamic (T98ss, QJT) — favor larger bets with polarized range, (c) paired boards — unique strategies around trips/quads, (d) monotone boards — nut advantage matters enormously. The bot's current board texture analysis may not distinguish these categories sharply enough.\n\n**3. SPR-Aware Strategy (from GTO Wizard):**\nStack-to-pot ratio fundamentally changes strategy: (a) SPR<3: commit-or-fold, (b) SPR 3-6: one-street decisions, (c) SPR>6: multi-street planning required. Many bots fail to adjust their bet sizing and commitment thresholds based on SPR.\n\n**4. Equity Realization (from GTO Wizard):**\nRaw equity ≠ realized equity. OOP realizes ~85-90% of equity vs IP's ~110%. Draw-heavy boards reduce equity realization for the non-initiative player. This is a critical factor the bot may underweight.\n\n**5. Blocker-Based Bluff Selection (from GTO Wizard):**\nOptimal bluff selection uses blockers to reduce opponent's value range. Key heuristics: (a) bluff with hands that block the nuts, (b) bluff with hands that unblock opponent folds, (c) avoid bluffing hands that block opponent bluffs (since they're less likely to call). reduce bluffs\n        profile[\"raise_size_bonus\"] = 0.06 * score\n        profile[\"call_threshold_delta\"] = 0.03 * score  # fold more marginal hands\n        profile[\"fold_threshold_delta\"] = -0.03 * score\n    elif is_aggressive and is_loose:\n        # Loose-aggressive maniac: call down wider, trap more\n        profile[\"type\"] = \"lag\"\n        profile[\"exploit_score\"] = score\n        profile[\"bluff_freq_bonus\"] = -0.10 * score  # bluff less\n        profile[\"raise_size_bonus\"] = 0.0\n        profile[\"call_threshold_delta\"] = -0.05 * score  # call lighter\n        profile[\"trap_defense_delta\"] = 0.06 * score\n    elif is_aggressive and not is_loose:\n        # Tight-aggressive: respect their raises, exploit with traps\n        profile[\"type\"] = \"tag\"\n        profile[\"exploit_score\"] = score\n        profile[\"bluff_freq_bonus\"] = -0.08 * score\n        profile[\"call_threshold_delta\"] = 0.04 * score  # fold more to their raises\n        profile[\"trap_defense_delta\"] = 0.05 * score\n    elif is_balanced:\n        # Balanced: minimal exploitation, just small adjustments\n        profile[\"type\"] = \"balanced\"\n        profile[\"exploit_score\"] = score * 0.3\n        profile[\"bluff_freq_bonus\"] = 0.02 * score\n        profile[\"raise_size_bonus\"] = 0.02 * score\n    elif check_rate > 0.55:\n        # Check-heavy opponent: probe bet more on checked rivers\n        profile[\"type\"] = \"check_heavy\"\n        profile[\"exploit_score\"] = score\n        profile[\"bluff_freq_bonus\"] = 0.10 * score\n        profile[\"raise_size_bonus\"] = 0.04 * score\n    \n    return profile\n```\n\n### Function 2: `get_exploit_adjustments(opp_profile, board_texture, spot_info, round_idx, value_profile)`\nReturns board-aware adjustments:\n```python\ndef get_exploit_adjustments(opp_profile, board_texture, spot_info, round_idx, value_profile):\n    \"\"\"Apply board-texture-aware modifications to opponent profile adjustments.\"\"\"\n    adj = dict(opp_profile)  # Copy base adjustments\n    score = opp_profile[\"exploit_score\"]\n    \n    if score <= 0 or board_texture is None:\n        return adj\n    \n    # Wet board vs tight opponent: bluff even more\n    if board_texture.get(\"dynamic\", False) and opp_profile[\"type\"] in (\"tight_passive\", \"check_heavy\"):\n        adj[\"bluff_freq_bonus\"] += 0.08 * score\n        adj[\"raise_size_bonus\"] += 0.04 * score\n    \n    # Paired board: exploit overfold caution\n    if board_texture.get(\"paired\", False):\n        adj[\"bluff_freq_bonus\"] += 0.05 * score\n    \n    # River: increase bluff vs check-heavy opponents\n    if round_idx == 3 and opp_profile[\"type\"] in (\"tight_passive\", \"check_heavy\"):\n        adj[\"bluff_freq_bonus\"] += 0.10 * score\n    \n    # Facing aggression from LAG: call down lighter\n    if spot_info.get(\"facing_postflop_aggression\", False) and opp_profile[\"type\"] == \"lag\":\n        adj[\"call_threshold_delta\"] -= 0.03 * score\n    \n    # Against stations: only value bet, no bluffs\n    if opp_profile[\"type\"] == \"station\" and value_profile is not None:\n        if value_profile.get(\"tier\") in (\"strong\", \"nut\"):\n            adj[\"raise_size_bonus\"] += 0.08 * score\n    \n    return adj\n```\n\n## Task 2: Integrate opponent profiling into strategy.py\n\n### 2a. Add imports\nIn strategy.py, add to the opponent import line:\n```python\nfrom opponent import build_opponent_model, analyze_current_spot, classify_opponent_profile, get_exploit_adjustments\n```\n\n### 2b. Add `anti_bot4_bonus` parameter to `choose_raise`\nAdd `anti_bot4_bonus=0.0` as a parameter to the `choose_raise` function signature (after `match_sizing_delta`). Inside choose_raise, add:\n```python\nratio += anti_bot4_bonus\n```\nright after the line `ratio += match_sizing_delta`.\n\n### 2c. Modify `allow_low_frequency_blocker_bluff` call signature\nIn `postflop.py`, add a `bluff_freq_bonus=0.0` parameter to `allow_low_frequency_blocker_bluff`. Modify the threshold calculation:\nChange the token/threshold logic to:\n```python\nthreshold = clamp(blocker_profile[\"score\"] * 35.0, 5.0, 18.0) + bluff_freq_bonus * 100.0\nreturn random.random() * 100 < threshold\n```\n(This matches v5's approach.)\n\n### 2d. Use profiling in get_action\nIn the `get_action` function, after computing opponent_model and n_hands (need to compute `n_hands = len(collect_latest_requests_by_hand(requests))`), add:\n```python\nopp_profile = classify_opponent_profile(opponent_model, n_hands)\n```\n\nAfter computing board_texture (around the value_profile computation), add:\n```python\nif board_texture is not None:\n    exploit_adj = get_exploit_adjustments(opp_profile, board_texture, spot_info, round_idx, value_profile)\nelse:\n    exploit_adj = opp_profile  # Use base adjustments\n```\n\nApply adjustments in these locations:\n1. **strong/medium thresholds** (around where `pressure_adjust` is applied):\n```python\nstrong -= exploit_adj[\"call_threshold_delta\"]\nmedium -= exploit_adj[\"call_threshold_delta\"] * 0.8\nstrong += exploit_adj[\"trap_defense_delta\"]\n```\n\n2. **Bluff thresholds** (where river_bluff_threshold, probe_fold_threshold, semi_bluff_threshold are computed):\n```python\nriver_bluff_threshold -= exploit_adj[\"bluff_freq_bonus\"]\nprobe_fold_threshold -= exploit_adj[\"bluff_freq_bonus\"]\nsemi_bluff_threshold -= exploit_adj[\"bluff_freq_bonus\"]\n```\n\n3. **choose_raise calls** — pass `anti_bot4_bonus=exploit_adj[\"raise_size_bonus\"]` to both choose_raise calls in get_action.\n\n4. **allow_low_frequency_blocker_bluff calls** — pass `bluff_freq_bonus=exploit_adj[\"bluff_freq_bonus\"]` as extra parameter.\n\n## CRITICAL RULES:\n- Do NOT change any thresholds, constants, or magic numbers. # Role
You are the Master Bot Architect for a Texas Hold'em poker AI. You are a world-class Prompt Engineer, Strategist, and Team Orchestrator.

Your goal is to:
1. Read the ratings data and analyze the current bot's performance. Understand the rating trend.

   - Remove or consolidate redundant entries.

(smaller bluffs are more EV-efficient in theory)\n- Continuation bet (c-bet) frequency: ~65-75% on favorable boards, ~40-50% on unfavorable\n- Check-raise frequency: ~12-18% with strong hands, ~5-10% as bluff\n\n### 2C: Bluff Frequency by Street\n- Flop bluff frequency: ~30-40% of air hands\n- Turn bluff frequency (after flop c-bet): ~40-50% (double barrel)\n- River bluff frequency: ~25-35% (triple barrel)\n- Adjust DOWN by 10-15% against calling stations (LP opponents)\n- Adjust UP by 10-15% against tight-passive (TP) opponents\n\n### 2D: Opponent-Adaptive Parameters\n- Against TAG opponents: increase call frequency by 15%, decrease bluff frequency by 20%\n- Against LAG opponents: increase value bet frequency by 25%, decrease bluff frequency by 30%\n- Against TP opponents: increase bluff frequency by 25%, increase steal attempts by 20%\n- Against LP opponents: increase value bet sizing by 20%, decrease bluff frequency by 40%\n\n### 2E: Monte Carlo Simulation Parameters\n- Default simulation hands: 500-800\n- Critical spot simulation hands: 1500-2500 (3x multiplier)\n- Early termination threshold: stop if equity < 0.15 or > 0.85 after 30% of runs\n- Range # Role
You are the Master Bot Architect for a Texas Hold'em poker AI. You are a world-class Prompt Engineer, Strategist, and Team Orchestrator.

# Essential Data Files
Read these files FIRST to understand the current state:
- `evolution_workspace/results/glicko_ratings.json` — All bot Glicko-2 ratings (r, rd, volatility)
- `evolution_workspace/results/rating_history.jsonl` — Rating snapshots over time (trend analysis)
- `evolution_workspace/experience_pool.md` — Accumulated strategic lessons from past generations
- `bots/claude_v{N}/` — Bot source code directories

Use `git log` and `git diff` to understand evolution history.

# Task
Your goal is to:
1. Read the ratings data and analyze the current bot's performance. Understand the rating trend.
2. Read the experience pool to learn from past iterations.
3. Read the current bot's source code and reference bots' code to identify weaknesses.
4. Update the Experience Pool by editing `evolution_workspace/experience_pool.md` directly:
   - Add new insights at the bottom.
   - Remove or consolidate redundant entries.
   - Keep the file concise (under 100 lines).
5. Dynamically assign Developer Sub-Agents (Workers) to implement your strategy.
6. You MUST STRICTLY divide your tasks into TWO distinct directions:
   - **Direction A (Algorithmic Logic Architect):** Method refactoring, logic additions, new evaluation functions, or fusing algorithms from reference bots.
   - **Direction B (Hyperparameter Tuner):** FORBIDDEN from altering logic. Only tune constants, thresholds, and magic numbers.
7. Write the exact, comprehensive prompt (`worker_prompt`) for each worker.

# Stagnation Decision
No stagnation detected. Continue from latest version.
If stagnation is detected, you can:
1. Set `"branch_from": "claude_v{N}"` to branch evolution from a different ancestor.
2. Choose the highest-rated non-stagnant bot, or a bot with a different strategy.
3. If no `branch_from` is set, evolution continues from the latest version.

=============================
# Role
You are the Master Bot Architect for a Texas Hold'em poker AI. You are a world-class Prompt Engineer, Strategist, and Team Orchestrator.

# Essential Data Files
Read these files FIRST to understand the current state:
- `evolution_workspace/results/glicko_ratings.json` — All bot Glicko-2 ratings (r, rd, volatility)
- `evolution_workspace/results/rating_history.jsonl` — Rating snapshots over time (trend analysis)
- `evolution_workspace/experience_pool.md` — Accumulated strategic lessons from past generations
- `bots/claude_v{N}/` — Bot source code directories

Use `git log` and `git diff` to understand evolution history.

# Task
Your goal is to:
1. Read the ratings data and analyze the current bot's performance. Understand the rating trend.
2. Read the experience pool to learn from past iterations.
3. Read the current bot's source code and reference bots' code to identify weaknesses.
4. Update the Experience Pool by editing `evolution_workspace/experience_pool.md` directly:
   - Add new insights at the bottom.
   - Remove or consolidate redundant entries.
   - Keep the file concise (under 100 lines).
5. Dynamically assign Developer Sub-Agents (Workers) to implement your strategy.
6. You MUST STRICTLY divide your tasks into TWO distinct directions:
   - **Direction A (Algorithmic Logic Architect):** Method refactoring, logic additions, new evaluation functions, or fusing algorithms from reference bots.
   - **Direction B (Hyperparameter Tuner):** FORBIDDEN from altering logic. Only tune constants, thresholds, and magic numbers.
7. Write the exact, comprehensive prompt (`worker_prompt`) for each worker.

# Stagnation Decision
No stagnation detected. Continue from latest version.
If stagnation is detected, you can:
1. Set `"branch_from": "claude_v{N}"` to branch evolution from a different ancestor.
2. Choose the highest-rated non-stagnant bot, or a bot with a different strategy.
3. If no `branch_from` is set, evolution continues from the latest version.

# Output Format
You MUST output your response containing exactly ONE JSON block formatted as follows:

    }
  ]

1. Output strictly valid JSON.
2. The `worker_prompt` you write for each worker will be fed DIRECTLY to that worker's LLM.
3. Explicitly enforce the boundaries: Logic Architects must not blindly mess with finely-tuned parameters, and Hyperparameter Tuners must not write new functions.
4. **TASK DIFFICULTY CONTROL**: Each task should involve modifying 1-3 specific functions. If previous generations had worker failures, split tasks into smaller, more focused units.
5. **FILE OWNERSHIP**: For each task, specify `target_files` — the files the worker should modify. Workers must NOT modify files outside their assigned `target_files`.
6. **STAGNATION AWARENESS**: If the rating trend shows no improvement, consider radically different approaches. Look at reference bots you haven't studied yet, or try combining features from multiple bots.

# Role
You are the Master Bot Architect for a Texas Hold'em poker AI. You are a world-class Prompt Engineer, Strategist, and Team Orchestrator.

# Essential Data Files

# Task
Your goal is to:
1. Read the ratings data and analyze the current bot's performance. Understand the rating trend.
2. Read the experience pool to learn from past iterations.
3. Read the current bot's source code and reference bots' code to identify weaknesses.

   - **Direction A (Algorithmic Logic Architect):** Method refactoring, logic additions, new evaluation functions, or fusing algorithms from reference bots.
   - **Direction B (Hyperparameter Tuner):** FORBIDDEN from altering logic. Only tune constants, thresholds, and magic numbers.

Port it EXACTLY from bot5:\n\n```python\ndef choose_overbet_river(\n    min_raise, my_chips, my_round_bet, to_call, pot,\n    win_rate, value_profile, board_texture, spot_info, opponent_model\n):\n    \"\"\"River overbet: 1.5-2.2x pot with NUT hands only.\"\"\"\n    if value_profile is None or value_profile[\"tier\"] != \"nut\":\n        return None\n    if board_texture is not None and board_texture[\"wetness\"] > 0.35:\n        return None\n    if pot < 400:\n        return None\n\n    pot_after_call = pot + to_call\n    ratio = 1.5 + 0.3 * max(0.0, win_rate - 0.70)\n    if not spot_info.get(\"has_position\", False):\n        ratio = max(1.3, ratio - 0.2)\n    ratio = min(ratio, 2.2)\n    amount = int(to_call + pot_after_call * ratio)\n\n    if amount >= my_chips:\n        return -2\n    amount = min(amount, my_chips - 1)\n    if amount <= to_call or amount < min_raise:\n        return None\n    return amount\n```\n\n## Change 2: Integrate River Overbet in `get_action()`\nIn `get_action()`, AFTER the line `anti_bot4 = ...` (or equivalent — after value_profile, board_texture, nutted_risk are computed, BEFORE the `if state[\"opponent_allin\"]:` block), add:\n\n```python\n    # River overbet with nut hands on dry boards\n    if round_idx == 3 and value_profile is not None and value_profile[\"tier\"] == \"nut\":\n        overbet = choose_overbet_river(\n            state[\"min_raise_action\"], my_chips, state[\"my_round_bet\"],\n            to_call, pot, win_rate, value_profile, board_texture, spot_info, opponent_model\n        )\n        if overbet is not None:\n            return overbet\n```\n\nPlace this right AFTER the `gift_balance = track_opponent_gift(...)` and `exploit_lambda = safe_exploitation_lambda(...)` lines, BEFORE the `strong = 0.69 if round_idx == 0 ...` thresholds block. This ensures nut hands on dry rivers get maximum value.\n\n## Change 3: Remove `bb_vs_raise` and `sb_vs_reraise` from `choose_preflop_spot_action()`\nIn `choose_preflop_spot_action()`, there are currently 4 branches:\n1. `sb_open` — KEEP AS IS\n2. `bb_vs_limp` — KEEP AS IS\n3. `bb_vs_raise` — DELETE THIS ENTIRE BLOCK (from `if spot_info[\"preflop_spot\"] == \"bb_vs_raise\":` to the end of that branch, approximately lines 639-665)\n4. `sb_vs_reraise` — DELETE THIS ENTIRE BLOCK (from `if spot_info[\"preflop_spot\"] == \"sb_vs_reraise\":` to the end of that branch, approximately lines 667-680)\n\nAfter removing these branches, the function should end with `return None` (matching bot5's approach). When these spots return None, `get_action()` will fall through to the GENERAL simulation-based path that uses win_rate, pot_odds, and opponent modeling — which is PROVEN superior to fixed preflop_strength thresholds.\n\n## Change 4: Fix `choose_raise()` — thin_cap, max_ratio, allow_river_overbet\nIn the `choose_raise()` function:\n\n### 4a. (2) Simplified from wetness-based formula to flat values 0.30/0.38. (3) These values are from bot5 (Rank 1).\n\n### 4c. Fix max_ratio (currently the `ratio = clamp(ratio, low_ratio, 1.45)` line):\nCHANGE FROM:\n```python\n    ratio = clamp(ratio, low_ratio, 1.45)\n```\nCHANGE TO:\n```python\n    max_ratio = 2.2 if (allow_river_overbet and round_idx == 3 and value_profile.get(\"tier\") == \"nut\") else 1.45\n    ratio = clamp(ratio, low_ratio, max_ratio)\n```\n\n### 4d. [MASTER (Try 1) PROMPT]
=============================
# Role
You are the Master Bot Architect for a Texas Hold'em poker AI. You are a world-class Prompt Engineer, Strategist, and Team Orchestrator.

# Essential Data Files
Read these files FIRST to understand the current state:
- `evolution_workspace/results/glicko_ratings.json` — All bot Glicko-2 ratings (r, rd, volatility)
- `evolution_workspace/results/rating_history.jsonl` — Rating snapshots over time (trend analysis)
- `evolution_workspace/experience_pool.md` — Accumulated strategic lessons from past generations
- `bots/claude_v{N}/` — Bot source code directories

Use `git log` and `git diff` to understand evolution history.

# Task
Your goal is to:
1. Read the ratings data and analyze the current bot's performance. Understand the rating trend.
2. Read the experience pool to learn from past iterations.
3. Read the current bot's source code and reference bots' code to identify weaknesses.
4. Update the Experience Pool by editing `evolution_workspace/experience_pool.md` directly:
   - Add new insights at the bottom.
   - Remove or consolidate redundant entries.
   - Keep the file concise (under 100 lines).
5. Dynamically assign Developer Sub-Agents (Workers) to implement your strategy.
6. You MUST STRICTLY divide your tasks into TWO distinct directions:
   - **Direction A (Algorithmic Logic Architect):** Method refactoring, logic additions, new evaluation functions, or fusing algorithms from reference bots.
   - **Direction B (Hyperparameter Tuner):** FORBIDDEN from altering logic. Only tune constants, thresholds, and magic numbers.
7. Write the exact, comprehensive prompt (`worker_prompt`) for each worker.

# Stagnation Decision
No stagnation detected. Continue from latest version.
If stagnation is detected, you can:
1. Set `"branch_from": "claude_v{N}"` to branch evolution from a different ancestor.
2. Choose the highest-rated non-stagnant bot, or a bot with a different strategy.
3. If no `branch_from` is set, evolution continues from the latest version.
